Here is the translation: And it has come to me in vision that I will complete this with this treatise, which is part of the work of hands, namely "surgery".
And because the work of hands is forgotten in our region and is strange to everything altogether, so the knowledge is perished and broken off, and nothing remains of it except for a few descriptions in books of the ancients that the hands have moved. And from this has come error and vanity, and are closed the intentions, and is alienated the knowledge.
It seems to me that I will bring it to life together with the ordering of this treatise according to the path of exposition and declaration and abbreviation. and I will bring together the forms of fire cauteries and other instruments of work with the adjustment of declaration and preparation for it, as is necessary.
And for that reason that no good masters of hands are found in our time, the art of medicine is estranged. And it is necessary for him who intervenes to master the science of anatomy, as Galen says, so that he knows the judgment of members, and their forms, and conjunctions, and separations, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and sinews and the number of vertebrae, and the arrangement and moving and resting muscles, and the origin of their issue.
And so Hippocrates says that the name with the name is much, and with the work is little. and indeed in the art of handcraft.
We tell you at the beginning of this book that whoever is not knowledgeable about the things previously mentioned should beware lest he make an error and kill people.
in such a way that I have seen many of those who interfere with this science and so abandon their knowledge and sense experience.
For I saw a foolish doctor who cut out the abscess of scrofula or collarbone from a woman and cut the arteries of the collarbone. Why so much blood issued forth that the woman fell dead between her hands.
And a certain wise man who treated an arrow wound on an old man's leg, and the arrow was large; so he took with him a piece of the bladder, and the man died inside three days.
And I had already been summoned to treat him, and saw the patient's condition and the size of the stone, and knew that if it was not removed he would die.
And a certain wise man who took care of the duke of our land who had his leg broken and with the breaking was wounded;
and the wise men, full of ignorance, set the breaking on top of the wound in such a way that it was firmly fixed, and left no room for healing, and left him thus at the end.
and he commanded that he not be loosened at all;
and remained thus so that the leg became entirely gangrened and the toes came to ruin.
I am called to come to him, and I hurry to come and untie the leg. and when I untied it so it was at peace and did not feel any pain.
But all the way the corruption had already been confirmed in the member, and could not be healed;
and the corruption did not cease to spread through the member until the member was completely lost.
And I saw another surgeon who burst an abscess that had become gangrenous, and then inflamed it by the wickedness of his authority.
For a gangrenous sore, when it is purged of melancholic humor, does not agree that one touches it with iron unless it is in such a place that one can entirely remove what is corrupted.
And therefore, dear son, you must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, one which has peril in several situations;
and I will show you in each place of this book where there is fear and peril.
For which it is necessary that you keep them for yourself, so that the foolish mouth cannot speak ill of you.
Take your arms in order, and begin to treat your patients lightly and firmly, and follow the best way so that by the grace of God you come to salvation and are praised.
and let go of the grievous illnesses of bad health;
and put away your doubts about what troubles you, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to the other of glory.
Galien says in some of his admonitions: Don't take on yourself a bad disease unless you're called a foolish doctor.
I have written this treatise according to three chapters.
The first chapters are about fire cauterizations and medical cauterizations with water, and the chapters are ordered from head to feet.
and about the forms of instruments, and of fixings for cauterizations, and of everything that is necessary in the work.
The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and about poultices and wounds, and about extracting arrows, and similar things;
and it is the chapters that are ordered and the shapes of the instruments.
The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things;
and it is the chapters ordered as far as the head, and the shapes of the instruments.
Furthermore, so that we may remember the work, it is necessary for me to say the quality of aid and detriment of each complexion.
I say that the quality of help, and of harm, is the longest word and subtlest science and secret responses;
and about these things many wise men spoke and agreed with them;
and I am not satisfied with their words, because I fear the length.
I say that fire-cautery helps universally to all constitutions where there is matter, except for two constitutions: it's to know warm complexion with regard to material, and dry complexion with regard to material.
In a warm and dry complexion together with material, some people divided and said that the fire cautery is a great help; and others said the opposite: that the fire cautery is not good for disease that comes from heat and dryness. For the nature of fire is hot, and should not be cured for a hot disease by heat or dryness;
and those who said the opposite say that the fire cautery makes great help for hot and dry diseases that come in the bodies of men. For when you consider the body of man and its moisture according to the nature of fire, you find the body cold.
And I agree with this word. For I have found it to be so on some occasions through experience.
And in any case, do not intervene except by one who has experimented with it, and who knows by long use the chapter of cauteries, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and the space of time;
We have no fear of other temperaments, especially in cold and moist diseases. And all the physicians assembled and agreed on the cautery.
And know, son, that fire cautery is among the secrets of cures, and of greater good than burning medicine.
For fire is simple, and does not come forth to another member unless it touches the one that is cauterized, and does no harm to any other member if it is not called upon.
Burning medicines come from member to member by applying, and bring grievous disease to the afflicted member; and it happens that the patient dies.
Fire, because of its height and the goodness of its substance, does not do this unless there is excessiveness.
And I have found this by experiment and the length of my service and study that I have put into the art, and it is based on the truth of things;
and therefore I excuse the length of my speech, for it does not please me that I take away from you the secret which is revealed by fire and the quality of work, how it repels the diseases of bodies, as philosophers say in demonstrating; Receive him in your thoughts.
And know, son, that they agreed on when the cauterizations should be done and chose precedents.

And never think thus, dear son, as foolish men do; for the disease that is cured by cauterization has no return. and they say so;

the treatment of chance by cauterization
When a chancre comes at the beginning, and you see it stop, then cauterize it with the cautery that seems like a circle, all around the border of the chancre.
And yet the sages say that one makes a fire cauterization in the middle of the sore;
and yet it does not seem good to me, for I fear that it will be ulcerated and corrupted, and I have already seen it happen at times;
and a more right thing is that he be cauterized around, at the cauterization which is called "circle", as we have said in many cauterizations.
When someone has a disease which is called "adubelati", and it delays in dying or because of the superfluity that it causes or because of the age of the patient when he is decrepit (that is to say, too old) and he has little blood, or because of the time; and you see hastening to die: then one cauterizes around with many small cauterizations in pricking; after that, let it be so. For it will hasten to die.
And if you see it piercing through the whole cautery, then heat the cautery with what is called "the form":
And put your hand in the midst of that disease which is called "adubelati" until the cauteries have pierced the kernel, and be such cauteries that the patient feels them outside in this way that the course of the purgation may be guided.
Afterward, care for him until he is perfectly healed.
Another manner of disease there is which is called "corrodens", and it is nothing else than a wasting away of the member, for it wastes away members just as fire dries out dry wood.

of fistula or whatever it may be Know that every wound or abscess, when it begins to fester, is universally called a "fistula", and similarly when it breaks open and flows.

and I will tell you of a fistula that occurred in a man's leg, so that you may take it as an example and aid in your work.
He was a young man around thirty years old who had a pain in his leg from a cause that came from within the body, so that the matters came out at the leg and became inflamed with a great abscess, and he had no reason to stop until it opened;
but the physician through their foolishness worked so much on the abscess that it opened, and there was a great deal of matter, and it became a fistula, and many ulcers came that all burst forth with pus and moisture from the body.
and many physicians had treated him for two years, and there was no benefit in the art of healing, until I was summoned, and I saw his leg and the remedies with which he was being treated, and what flowed from the ulcers with great corruption. and the skin of the young person became red and had a citrine color.
I set up a tent in one of these perforations, and then searched all the perforations, and found that one was coming against another from all parts of the leg.
So I hastened and cut into one of the ulcers until I discovered a part of the bone, and I found it corrupted and perforated, and the corruption came as far as the bone inside.
I saw what appeared to be the corrupted bone and thought there was no other corruption except for that which I removed.
and I began to heal the wound with medicines over a long time, and could not close it.

of wound and dislocation together
When a wound comes with the dislocation and one seeks to restore it, many times it happens that the patient dies:
if you are not modest in the treatment, if you are not wise in the art and have not used it for a long time, and if you are not pitiful and merciful and tardy, nor too bold;

and when the limb is at rest, administer soothing things to abscesses hot, and treat the wound as it should be, with ointments dried.
